> #include <stdio.h>
> #include <stdlib.h>
> 
> // Accidentially wrote this in C, but as we all know, C++ is a superset of C,
> // so it's definitely a C++ program as well.
> 
> int main(int argc, char const *argv[])
> {
>     if (argc > 1) {
>         int number = atoi(argv[1]);
>         printf("Factors of %d:", number);
>         for (int i = 1; i <= number; i++) {
>             if (number % i == 0) {
>                 printf(" %d", i);
>             }
>         }
>         printf("\n");
>     } else {
>         printf("Mate. I need a number.\n");
>     }
> }
> EOF

Type 'zypper help' to get a list of global options and commands.

In case 'purge' is not a typo it's probably not a built-in command, but provided as a subcommand or plug-in (see 'zypper help subcommand').
In this case a specific package providing the subcommand needs to be installed first. Those packages are often named 'zypper-purge' or 'zypper-purge-plugin'.

localhost:~/programs # cat << EOF > ~/programs/factorinator.cpp
> #include <stdio.h>
> #include <stdlib.h>
> 
> // Accidentially wrote this in C, but as we all know, C++ is a superset of C,
> // so it's definitely a C++ program as well.
> 
> int main(int argc, char const *argv[])
> {
>     if (argc > 1) {
>         int number = atoi(argv[1]);
>         printf("Factors of %d:", number);
>         for (int i = 1; i <= number; i++) {
>             if (number % i == 0) {
>                 printf(" %d", i);
>             }
>         }
>         printf("\n");
>     } else {
>         printf("Mate. I need a number.\n");
>     }
> }
> EOF
